'To find out how many children got off the bus at the bus stop, we need to subtract the number of children left on the bus from the initial number of children on the bus.\n\nInitial number of children on the bus = 43\nNumber of children left on the bus = 21\n\nNumber of children who got off the bus = Initial number of children on the bus - Number of children left on the bus\nNumber of children who got off the bus = 43 - 21\nNumber of children who got off the bus = 22\n\nTherefore, 22 children got off the bus at the bus stop.'
"Let's assume that x children got off the bus at the bus stop. \n\nInitially, there were 28 children on the bus. \nAfter 82 children got on the bus, the total number of children on the bus became 28 + 82 = 110. \nAfter some children got off the bus, there were 30 children on the bus. \n\nSo, we can write the equation: \n110 - x = 30 \n\nTo solve for x, we subtract 30 from both sides of the equation: \n110 - 30 - x = 30 - 30 \n80 - x = 0 \n\nNext, we subtract 80 from both sides of the equation: \n80 - x - 80 = 0 - 80 \n-x = -80 \n\nFinally, we multiply both sides of the equation by -1 to solve for x: \n(-1)(-x) = (-1)(-80) \nx = 80 \n\nTherefore, 80 children got off the bus at the bus stop. \n\nTo find the difference between the number of children who got on the bus and those who got off, we subtract the number of children who got off from the number of children who got on: \n82 - 80 = 2 \n\nTherefore, 2 more children got on the bus than those who got off."

Therefore, the remaining x - 38 students suggested other types of food.\n\nWe also know that the total number of choices was 66. This means that the number of students who suggested other types of food (x - 38) must equal the number of choices that were not suggested.\n\nSo, the number of choices that were not suggested is 66 - (x - 38).\n\nSince the rest of the students did not participate in suggesting new food items, the number of choices that were not suggested must equal the number of students who did not participate. Therefore, we can set up the following equation:\n\n66 - (x - 38) = 450 - x\n\nSimplifying the equation, we get:\n\n66 - x + 38 = 450 - x\n\nCombining like terms, we get:\n\n104 - x = 450 - x\n\nAdding x to both sides of the equation, we get:\n\n104 = 450\n\nThis is not a possible solution, as it implies that 104 is equal to 450, which is not true.\n\nTherefore, there is no solution to this problem."

"Let's assume that Nell gave x baseball cards and y Ace cards to Jeff.\n\nBefore giving any cards to Jeff, Nell had 309 baseball cards and 356 Ace cards.\nAfter giving x baseball cards to Jeff, Nell has 309 - x baseball cards left.\nAfter giving y Ace cards to Jeff, Nell has 356 - y Ace cards left.\n\nAccording to the given information, Nell now has 415 baseball cards and Ace cards left. So we can write the following equation:\n\n309 - x + 356 - y = 415\n\nSimplifying the equation, we get:\n\n665 - x - y = 415\n\nRearranging the equation, we get:\n\nx + y = 665 - 415\nx + y = 250\n\nNow, we need to find the difference between the number of baseball cards and Ace cards Nell has left. So we subtract the number of Ace cards from the number of baseball cards:\n\n(309 - x) - (356 - y) = 309 - 356 + y - x\n(309 - x) - (356 - y) = -47 + y - x\n\nWe know that Nell has more baseball cards than Ace cards, so the difference should be positive. Therefore, we can write:\n\n-47 + y - x > 0\n\nSimplifying the inequality, we get:\n\ny - x > 47\n\nSo, Nell has at least 47 more Ace cards than baseball cards."

So, the total amount he earns in one harvest season is:\n\n$1357/week * 223 weeks = $302,411\n\nNow, to find out how much money Lewis will earn if he works for 73 harvest seasons, we multiply the total amount earned in one harvest season by the number of harvest seasons:\n\n$302,411/harvest season * 73 harvest seasons = $22,079,003\n\nTherefore, Lewis will earn $22,079,003 if he works for 73 harvest seasons, earning $1357 per week for 223 weeks per harvest season.'

"Let's break down the information given in the question:\n\n- Initially, there were 36 children on the bus.\n- 68 children got off the bus at the bus stop.\n- Some more children got on the bus.\n- After all the changes, there were 12 children left on the bus.\n\nTo find out how many more children got off the bus than got on, we need to calculate the difference between the number of children who got off and the number of children who got on.\n\nInitially, there were 36 children on the bus. 68 children got off the bus at the bus stop. So, the number of children who got off is 68.\n\nAfter the children got off, there were 12 children left on the bus. Let's assume the number of children who got on the bus is x.\n\nTherefore, the equation representing the situation is:\n36 - 68 + x = 12\n\nSimplifying the equation:\n-32 + x = 12\n\nAdding 32 to both sides of the equation:\nx = 44\n\nSo, 44 children got on the bus.\n\nTo find out how many more children got off the bus than got on, we subtract the number of children who got on from the number of children who got off:\n68 - 44 = 24\n\nTherefore, 24 more children got off the bus than got on."

"Let's assume that Julia played with x kids on Monday and y kids on Tuesday. \n\nAccording to the given information, Julia played with a total of 38 kids over both days. So, we can write the equation:\n\nx + y = 38   ...........(1)\n\nAlso, it is given that Julia played with 19 kids on Monday and 18 kids on Tuesday. So, we can write another equation:\n\nx = 19   ...........(2)\ny = 18   ...........(3)\n\nFrom equation (2), we know that x = 19. Substituting this value in equation (1), we get:\n\n19 + y = 38\n\nSimplifying the equation, we find:\n\ny = 38 - 19\ny = 19\n\nSo, Julia played with 19 kids on Tuesday.\n\nTo find the difference in the number of kids Julia played with on Monday and Tuesday, we subtract the number of kids on Tuesday from the number of kids on Monday:\n\nDifference = Number of kids on Monday - Number of kids on Tuesday\nDifference = 19 - 18\nDifference = 1\n\nTherefore, Julia played with 1 more kid on Monday than on Tuesday."

"Let's assume that each bag has x number of cookies.\n\nSince there are 26 bags, the total number of cookies in all the bags is 26x.\n\nWe also know that there are 15 candies.\n\nSo, the total number of cookies and candies is 26x + 15.\n\nAccording to the given information, the total number of cookies and candies is 52.\n\nTherefore, we can write the equation as:\n\n26x + 15 = 52\n\nNow, let's solve this equation to find the value of x.\n\nSubtracting 15 from both sides of the equation:\n\n26x = 52 - 15\n26x = 37\n\nDividing both sides of the equation by 26:\n\nx = 37/26\n\nSimplifying the fraction:\n\nx = 1.42\n\nTherefore, each bag has approximately 1.42 cookies.\n\nSince we cannot have a fraction of a cookie, we can conclude that each bag has 1 cookie."

"Let's break down the information given in the question:\n\nInitially, there were 22 children on the bus.\nAt the bus stop, 40 children got on the bus.\nAfter the bus stop, there were only 2 children on the bus.\n\nTo find out how many children got off the bus at the bus stop, we need to subtract the number of children who were on the bus after the bus stop from the total number of children who got on the bus at the bus stop.\n\nTotal number of children on the bus after the bus stop = 2\nTotal number of children who got on the bus at the bus stop = 40\n\nNumber of children who got off the bus at the bus stop = Total number of children who got on the bus at the bus stop - Total number of children on the bus after the bus stop\n= 40 - 2\n= 38\n\nTherefore, 38 children got off the bus at the bus stop."

'To find out how many more Ace cards than baseball cards Nell has after giving some to Jeff, we need to calculate the difference between the number of Ace cards and the number of baseball cards.\n\nInitially, Nell had 246 baseball cards and 214 Ace cards. After giving some cards to Jeff, she now has 404 baseball cards and 495 Ace cards.\n\nTo find out how many cards Nell gave to Jeff, we can subtract the current number of cards from the initial number of cards for each type:\n\nBaseball cards given to Jeff = 246 - 404 = -158\nAce cards given to Jeff = 214 - 495 = -281\n\nSince we cannot have a negative number of cards given, it means that Nell received cards from Jeff instead of giving them. Therefore, we need to add the absolute values of these negative numbers to the current number of cards:\n\nNew number of baseball cards = 404 + |-158| = 404 + 158 = 562\nNew number of Ace cards = 495 + |-281| = 495 + 281 = 776\n\nNow, we can calculate the difference between the number of Ace cards and the number of baseball cards:\n\n776 - 562 = 214\n\nTherefore, Nell has 214 more Ace cards than baseball cards.'

'To calculate the total number of nails needed, we need to find the number of nails required for the large planks and the number of nails required for the small planks separately.\n\nFor the large planks:\n- John needs 12 large planks of wood.\n- Each large plank needs 15 nails to be secured.\nTherefore, the total number of nails needed for the large planks is 12 x 15 = 180 nails.\n\nFor the small planks:\n- John needs 10 small planks of wood.\n- Each small plank needs 5 nails to be secured.\nTherefore, the total number of nails needed for the small planks is 10 x 5 = 50 nails.\n\nTo find the total number of nails needed for the walls of the house, we add the number of nails needed for the large planks and the number of nails needed for the small planks:\n180 + 50 = 230 nails.\n\nTherefore, John needs 230 nails to secure the large and small planks for the walls of the house.'
'To find out how many more crayons Paul gave to his friends than those he lost, we need to subtract the number of crayons he lost from the number of crayons he gave to his friends.\n\nNumber of crayons Paul gave to his friends = 571\nNumber of crayons Paul lost = 161\n\nNumber of crayons Paul gave to his friends - Number of crayons Paul lost = 571 - 161 = 410\n\nTherefore, Paul gave 410 more crayons to his friends than those he lost.'

'To find the total number of visitors to the Buckingham Palace within a 57-day period, we need to consider the number of visitors on each day.\n\nOn the first day, there were 557 visitors.\nOn the second day, there were 188 visitors.\nOn the third day, there were 557 visitors.\nOn the fourth day, there were 188 visitors.\nAnd so on...\n\nWe can see that the number of visitors alternates between 557 and 188 each day.\n\nTo find the total number of visitors within 57 days, we need to determine how many times the pattern of 557 and 188 repeats, and then add any remaining days.\n\nThe pattern of 557 and 188 repeats every 2 + 2 = 4 days (2 days of 557 visitors and 2 days of 188 visitors).\n\nSo, within 57 days, there are 57 / 4 = 14 complete patterns.\n\nWithin these 14 complete patterns, there are 14 * 2 = 28 days with 557 visitors.\nAnd there are 14 * 2 = 28 days with 188 visitors.\n\nNow, we need to consider the remaining days.\n\nThere are 57 - (14 * 4) = 57 - 56 = 1 remaining day.\n\nSince the pattern of 557 and 188 alternates, the remaining day will have 557 visitors.\n\nTherefore, within 57 days, there are:\n28 days with 557 visitors\n28 days with 188 visitors\n1 day with 557 visitors\n\nTo find the total number of visitors, we can calculate:\n(28 * 557) + (28 * 188) + 557 = 15616 + 5264 + 557 = 21437\n\nSo, within 57 days, a total of 21,437 visitors visited the Buckingham Palace.'
'To find out how many more chocolate chip cookies Helen baked yesterday compared to today, we need to subtract the number of chocolate chip cookies she baked today from the number she baked yesterday.\n\nYesterday, Helen baked 197 chocolate chip cookies.\nToday, Helen baked 66 chocolate chip cookies.\n\nTo find the difference, we subtract the number of chocolate chip cookies baked today from the number baked yesterday:\n\n197 - 66 = 131\n\nTherefore, Helen baked 131 more chocolate chip cookies yesterday compared to today.'

'Faye has 35 packs of pencils, and each pack contains 4 pencils. So, the total number of pencils Faye has is 35 packs * 4 pencils/pack = 140 pencils.\n\nFaye wants to place 2 pencils in each row. To find out how many rows she can make, we need to divide the total number of pencils by the number of pencils in each row.\n\nNumber of rows = Total number of pencils / Number of pencils in each row\nNumber of rows = 140 pencils / 2 pencils/row\nNumber of rows = 70 rows\n\nTherefore, Faye can make 70 rows with her pencils.'

So, the weight of Marco\'s dad\'s strawberries and Marco\'s strawberries together is 15 + x pounds.\n\nIt is also given that together their strawberries weighed 37 pounds. So, we can write the equation:\n\n15 + x = 37\n\nTo find the value of x, we need to isolate it on one side of the equation. So, the number of pages of math homework she had to complete is x + 3.\nThe total number of pages Rachel had to complete is the sum of the pages of math and reading homework, which is x + (x + 3).\nWe know that Rachel had to complete 8 pages of math homework, so we can set up the equation:\nx + (x + 3) = 8\nSimplifying the equation, we get:\n2x + 3 = 8\nSubtracting 3 from both sides, we get:\n2x = 5\nDividing both sides by 2, we get:\nx = 2.5\nSince we can't have a fraction of a page, we can conclude that Rachel had to complete 2 pages of reading homework.\nTherefore, the total number of pages Rachel had to complete is 2 + (2 + 3) = 2 + 5 = 7 pages."

"The maximum seating capacity of the program is 44 people. This means that only 44 people can physically sit in the program at one time.\n\nWe know that there were 61 parents in the program and 177 pupils. However, since the program can only seat 44 people, not all parents and pupils can be seated at the same time.\n\nTo determine the total number of people present in the program, we need to consider the maximum seating capacity and the number of parents and pupils separately.\n\nSince the program can only seat 44 people, we can assume that all 44 seats are occupied by either parents or pupils. Let's assume that all 44 seats are occupied by parents.\n\nThis means that there are 44 parents seated in the program. Since there were originally 61 parents in the program, 61 - 44 = 17 parents cannot be seated.\n\nNow, let's consider the pupils. Since all 44 seats are occupied by parents, there are no seats left for the pupils. Therefore, none of the 177 pupils can be seated.\n\nTo summarize:\n- 44 parents can be seated in the program.\n- 17 parents cannot be seated.\n- None of the 177 pupils can be seated.\n\nTherefore, the total number of people present in the program is 44 parents + 0 pupils = 44 people."

'In the morning, Jack received 4 emails and sent 2 letters. Therefore, he had a net increase of 4 - 2 = 2 emails.\n\nIn the afternoon, Jack received 6 emails and sent 8 letters. Therefore, he had a net decrease of 6 - 8 = -2 emails.\n\nTo find the total number of emails Jack sent in the day, we need to add the net increases and decreases together.\n\nNet increase in the morning = 2 emails\nNet decrease in the afternoon = -2 emails\n\nTotal emails sent = Net increase in the morning + Net decrease in the afternoon\nTotal emails sent = 2 + (-2)\nTotal emails sent = 0\n\nTherefore, Jack did not send any emails throughout the day.'

"Let's break down the information given in the hint and question:\n\n1. There were originally 13 roses in the vase.\n2. Jessica cut some roses from her flower garden.\n3. Jessica's flower garden had a total of 12 roses.\n4. After cutting the roses, Jessica placed them in the vase.\n5. The vase now contains 21 roses.\n6. The question is asking for the number of roses left in Jessica's flower garden.\n\nTo find the number of roses left in Jessica's flower garden, we need to subtract the number of roses she placed in the vase from the total number of roses in her garden.\n\nWe know that there were originally 13 roses in the vase, and now there are 21 roses in the vase. This means that Jessica placed 21 - 13 = 8 roses in the vase.\n\nSince Jessica's flower garden originally had 12 roses, and she placed 8 roses in the vase, there are 12 - 8 = 4 roses left in her flower garden.\n\nTherefore, there are 4 roses left in Jessica's flower garden."

"Let's assume that Adam has x apples.\nAccording to the information given, Jackie has x + 8 apples.\nTogether, Adam and Jackie have x + (x + 8) = 2x + 8 apples.\nIt is also given that He has 9 apples more than Adam and Jackie together do.\nSo, He has (2x + 8) + 9 = 2x + 17 apples.\nWe know that together Adam and Jackie have 12 apples.\nTherefore, 2x + 8 = 12.\nSubtracting 8 from both sides, we get 2x = 4.\nDividing both sides by 2, we get x = 2.\nSo, Adam has 2 apples.\nJackie has x + 8 = 2 + 8 = 10 apples.\nAnd He has 2x + 17 = 2(2) + 17 = 4 + 17 = 21 apples.\nTherefore, He has 21 apples."

"Let's assume that the initial number of apples on Rachel's tree was x.\n\nRachel picked 6 ripe apples from the tree, so the number of ripe apples remaining on the tree is x - 6.\n\nThe tree also has 4 unripe apples, so the total number of apples remaining on the tree is (x - 6) + 4.\n\nAccording to the information given, the tree now has 2 ripe apples, so we can set up the equation:\n\n(x - 6) + 4 = 2\n\nSimplifying the equation, we get:\n\nx - 6 + 4 = 2\nx - 2 = 2\nx = 2 + 2\nx = 4\n\nTherefore, the initial number of apples on Rachel's tree was 4."

Therefore, we cannot compare the number of pastries not sold with the number of cakes not sold.\n\nHowever, if we compare the number of pastries sold with the number of cakes sold, we can see that Baker sold 18 more pastries than cakes (88 - 70 = 18).\n\nTherefore, Baker made 18 more pastries than cakes.'

"Based on the given information, we can deduce the following:\n\n1. Adam has 4 more apples than Jackie.\n2. Adam and Jackie together have 14 apples.\n3. Bob has 6 apples more than Adam and Jackie combined.\n\nLet's assume Jackie has x apples. Since Adam has 4 more apples than Jackie, Adam has (x + 4) apples.\n\nTogether, Adam and Jackie have 14 apples. So, the equation becomes:\n(x + x + 4) = 14.\n\nSimplifying the equation, we get:\n2x + 4 = 14.\n\nSubtracting 4 from both sides, we have:\n2x = 10.\n\nDividing both sides by 2, we find that:\nx = 5.\n\nTherefore, Jackie has 5 apples and Adam has (5 + 4) = 9 apples.\n\nBob has 6 apples more than Adam and Jackie combined. So, Bob has (5 + 9 + 6) = 20 apples.\n\nTherefore, Bob has 20 apples."

'To find the total number of sacks of oranges they will have after 26 days of harvest, we need to calculate the number of sacks of ripe oranges and unripe oranges separately, and then add them together.\n\nThe number of sacks of ripe oranges harvested per day is given as 28. So, in 26 days, they will harvest 28 * 26 = 728 sacks of ripe oranges.\n\nSimilarly, the number of sacks of unripe oranges harvested per day is given as 52. So, in 26 days, they will harvest 52 * 26 = 1352 sacks of unripe oranges.\n\nNow, to find the total number of sacks of oranges, we add the number of sacks of ripe oranges and unripe oranges together: 728 + 1352 = 2080.\n\nTherefore, after 26 days of harvest, they will have a total of 2080 sacks of oranges.'
"Let's assume that Adam has x apples. \n\nAccording to the first hint, Adam and Jackie have a total of 6 apples. So, we can write the equation: x + Jackie's apples = 6.\n\nAccording to the second hint, Adam has 4 apples less than what Adam and Jackie have together. So, we can write the equation: x = (x + Jackie's apples) - 4.\n\nNow, let's substitute the value of (x + Jackie's apples) from the first equation into the second equation: x = 6 - 4.\n\nSimplifying the equation, we get: x = 2.\n\nTherefore, Adam has 2 apples."

We can do this by dividing both sides of the equation by 7:\n14/7 = Width\n\nSimplifying the equation:\n2 = Width\n\nTherefore, the width of Jesse's room is 2 feet."

"Let's assume the number of boys in the school is x.\nAccording to the information given, there are 868 girls and 281 more girls than boys.\nSo, the number of girls can be represented as x + 281.\n\nThe total number of students in the school can be calculated by adding the number of girls and boys together.\nTherefore, the total number of students in the school is x + (x + 281).\n\nWe know that the total number of girls in the school is 868.\nSo, we can write the equation as:\nx + (x + 281) = 868\n\nSimplifying the equation, we get:\n2x + 281 = 868\n\nSubtracting 281 from both sides of the equation, we get:\n2x = 587\n\nDividing both sides of the equation by 2, we get:\nx = 293\n\nTherefore, the number of boys in the school is 293.\n\nTo find the total number of pupils in the school, we need to add the number of girls and boys together:\nTotal number of pupils = Number of girls + Number of boys\nTotal number of pupils = 868 + 293\nTotal number of pupils = 1161\n\nSo, there are 1161 pupils in the school."
"Let's assume that Zachary did x push-ups.\nAccording to the information given, David did 49 more push-ups than Zachary, so David did x + 49 push-ups.\nThe total number of push-ups done by David and Zachary is x + (x + 49) = 2x + 49.\nWe also know that David did 51 push-ups, so we can set up the equation:\n2x + 49 = 51\nSubtracting 49 from both sides of the equation, we get:\n2x = 2\nDividing both sides of the equation by 2, we get:\nx = 1\nTherefore, Zachary did 1 push-up.\nThe total number of push-ups done by David and Zachary is 1 + (1 + 49) = 1 + 50 = 51.\nSo, David and Zachary did 51 push-ups altogether."

"To solve this problem, we can use algebra. Let's assume that Matthew gave x crackers to each of his friends.\n\nSince Matthew had 24 crackers initially and gave x crackers to each of his 3 friends, he gave a total of 3x crackers to his friends.\n\nAfter giving the crackers to his friends, Matthew still had 17 crackers left. So we can write the equation:\n\n24 - 3x = 17\n\nTo solve for x, we can subtract 17 from both sides of the equation:\n\n24 - 17 = 3x\n\n7 = 3x\n\nNow, we can divide both sides of the equation by 3 to solve for x:\n\n7/3 = x\n\nx ≈ 2.33\n\nSince we can't have a fraction of a cracker, we need to round x to the nearest whole number. Therefore, Matthew gave each of his friends 2 crackers."
